OTHER ANCESTRIES
The following section provides context for how existing D&D 
ancestries are represented on the island of Obojima. None of the 
below naturally exist in the world of Obojima but could come to 
exist through other means.
To play one of these existing D&D ancestries 
you must either use the charts below to define 
your character’s origins–or create a unique 
origin of your own design.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

The section below details eleven new subclasses intertwined with the island of Obojima, its culture, 
and its creatures. These variants of the classic archetypes are not the only character types you’ll 
find on the island, but they do provide a playstyle that feels uniquely Obojiman.
SUBCLASSES
The darker the 
amber tones,  
the riper it is!
Only a Belly 
Brewer would 
eat the hard, 
bitter rind of a 
pyramid melon.
BELLY BREWER
These Barbarians are masters of brewing potions on the fly—
directly in their guts! While others must painstakingly prepare 
potions with finesse, Belly Brewers channel their inner hunger 
to unlock the latent magic within raw ingredients without  
any preparation. 
Those born with the rumble in their belly often find that 
regular food can’t quite satisfy—they require something more 
unusual. A generation ago, a handful of adventurous eaters with 
"the appetite" set out to find a way to appease their seemingly 
insatiable hunger. This is how they discovered “belly brewing.” 
When certain morsels were consumed together, they not only 
quieted the rumble for a time but also yielded the potion-like 
effects that Belly Brewers have since come to be known for.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 3: Belly Concoction 
You learn the hard-earned skill of belly brewing, an arcane 
technique in which you swallow, mix, and brew magical 
concoctions inside your gut to create a number of unique effects.
When you enter your Rage, you focus your energy to harness 
and activate the effects of a belly concoction. Choose one of the 
following types of belly concoctions: Combat, Utility, or Whimsy. 
You gain the benefits associated with the chosen type, as 
detailed below. You can change your belly concoction to a 
different type each time you enter your Rage.
Combat—Your body undergoes a unique change, which 
magically alters your physical form, giving it the characteristics 
of rubber. While in this elastic state, you can take a Reaction 
when you are hit by a ranged attack, deflecting it with your 
belly. When you do so, the damage you take from the attack  
is reduced by 1d12 plus your Constitution modifier and  
Barbarian level.
Additionally, immediately before you make a melee attack roll 
with a weapon or an Unarmed Strike on your turn, you can take 
a Bonus Action to stretch your arms, increasing your reach by 5 
feet for the rest of the turn. The first time you hit a target while 
your arms are stretched in this way, the attack deals an extra 
1d6 damage of the weapon’s type.
Utility—The bubbling elixir in your stomach is perfectly mixed to 
dissolve and absorb anything you are able to swallow. As a 
Bonus Action, you can consume any object that can fit in your 
mouth. If the object isn’t a magic item, you can expend one of 
your Hit Dice as part of this Bonus Action to heal yourself. Roll 
the die and add your Constitution modifier; you regain a number 
of Hit Points equal to the total (minimum of 1). Swallowing an 
object in this way destroys it, provided it isn’t magical. You can 
use this feature a number of times equal to your Constitution 
modifier, and you regain all expended uses when you finish a 
Long Rest.
Whimsy—You focus on the magical brew inside you, only to 
exhibit an array of strange and unruly effects. While in this state, 
you gain one of the following effects of your choice at the start of 
each of your turns:
• You teleport to an unoccupied space you can see within 10 feet 
of you.
• You take 1d4 Necrotic damage; the next ability check you  
make before the end of your turn gains a bonus equal to the 
number rolled.
• You can immediately take the Help action as a Bonus Action.
Additionally, you gain a random visual effect that accompanies 
the other whimsical features. For example, your hair might turn 
to moss, a spectral bird might circle above your head, or a tattoo 
of a dancing man might appear on your skin and move about 
your body.
Level 3: Side Effects
You gain a number of magical side effects due to the countless 
magical ingredients you’ve ingested. You know the Prestidigitation* 
and Thaumaturgy* cantrips. Constitution is your spellcasting ability 
for these spells.
Level 6: Quick Brew
You’ve learned how to better control the effects your belly 
concoction produces. Choose a common potion that one would 
normally consume. You can activate the effects of the chosen 
potion as a Bonus Action. Once you activate it, you can’t do so 
again until you finish a Long Rest. If the potion’s effects require a 
saving throw, the DC equals 8 plus your Constitution modifier 
and Proficiency Bonus.
Whenever you gain a Barbarian level, you can replace your 
chosen potion with a different one, provided it is also a common 
potion that one would normally consume.
An alternate way of using this feature is to allow 
the player to choose only from the potion recipes 
they know. If the Belly Brewer hasn’t learned any 
potion recipes, the GM should provide a list of ten 
options to choose from.
Level 10: Lingering Effects
The ever-present concoction in your stomach is now so potent it 
grants you benefits even when you aren’t raging. When you 
finish a Long Rest, choose one of the following conditions: 
Blinded, Charmed, Exhaustion, Frightened, Paralyzed, Petrified, 
Poisoned, Prone, Restrained, or Stunned. You have Advantage 
on saving throws against that condition until you choose a 
different one with this feature.
Level 14: Mighty Quick Brew
You learn an additional common potion as well as an uncommon 
potion, using your Quick Brew feature. Whenever you gain a 
Barbarian level, you can replace one of these potions with a 
different one, provided it is also a common or uncommon potion, 
respectively, that one would normally consume.
BARBARIAN


--- PAGE BREAK ---

COLLEGE OF MASKS 
To be a Bard from the College of Masks is to be a theater actor 
capable of losing themselves in a role by using masks they imbue 
with magic. Through these masks, Bards can mimic others and 
even take on attributes of the personas their masks depict.
To see the world through another’s eyes. To show the world a 
face not your own. To become someone else. These are the 
actor’s pursuits. Some local players might putter about on the 
stage as a hobby or distraction, but not Bards of the College of 
Masks. Like liquid bronze being poured into a mold, these actors 
have turned their sense of self into a malleable thing able to 
transform themselves into someone else.
Tradition of Performance
The College of Masks not only describes the Bard but also refers 
to an Obojiman theater tradition in which a solitary masked 
actor plays out a story from the island’s myths and folktales. 
These stories feature a set of archetypal characters such as the 
Old Man, the Fish, and the Demon, among others. Throughout 
the show, the actor artfully shifts between masks depicting each 
character. Each performance offers something special, as no two 
are ever the same.
Level 3: Tools of Performance
You gain the ability to weave arcane boons into theater masks, 
which grant you abilities while you wear them. You craft two 
masks of your choice from the “Masks” section later in this 
subclass’s description. You craft one additional mask of your 
choice when you reach Bard levels 7, 11, and 15. Each time you 
craft a new mask, you can also replace one mask you’ve already 
crafted with a different one.
While wearing a mask, you gain the abilities granted by it. You 
can don or swap masks as a Utilize action or Bonus Action. If an 
ability from a mask requires a saving throw, the DC equals your 
Bard spell save DC.
Level 3: Copycat
You gain the ability to quickly shift your appearance to match 
that of another person. As a Magic action, you can expend one 
use of Bardic Inspiration to cast the Alter Self* spell, using the 
spell’s Change Appearance option to transform into another 
Humanoid you have seen. When cast in this way, the spell has 
the following changes:
• It doesn’t require Concentration.
• You gain 5 Temporary Hit Points, and the spell ends early if you 
lose all these Hit Points or die.
• You gain new equipment associated with the target and known 
to be in its possession, such as its clothing, armor, weapons, 
and other small belongings. Any equipment gained in this way 
vanishes when the spell ends and has no magical properties, 
even if the original items used by the target do.
Any equipment you were wearing or carrying merges into your 
new form, and you can't activate, use, wield, or otherwise 
benefit from any of it.
 The rubble golem  
is a common character 
in masked theater 
performances.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 6:  
Many-Masked Performance
Over the course of 1 minute, you can engage in a captivating 
performance and attempt to cause nearby creatures to have the 
Charmed, Frightened, or Unconscious condition (your choice). 
Choose a number of creatures up to your Bard level within 60 
feet of you that can hear you. When the performance ends, each 
target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw against your 
Bard spell save DC or have the chosen condition for 10 minutes. 
An affected target can repeat the save whenever it takes 
damage, ending the effect on itself on a success.
Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you 
finish a Long Rest.
Level 14: Gift of Theater
You gain the ability to give one of your masks from your Tools of 
Performance feature to an ally within 5 feet of you. As a Magic 
action, you temporarily release the incantation that binds the 
mask to you, allowing one of your allies to use it. The mask can 
be used in this way for 1 minute, and only one ally can be 
designated to use it.
Once you’ve given an ally a mask, you can’t do so again until 
you finish a Short or Long Rest.
MASKS
Demon (Prerequisite: Level 5+ Bard).  
While wearing this mask, you gain the following benefits:
• Arcane Memory. As a Magic action, you can expend a spell slot 
to magically learn whether a creature or object you specify 
has been within 20 feet of your current location in the past 
24 hours. If you expend a spell slot of level 3 or higher, you 
receive a brief vision of the creature or object while it was 
there, and you learn the exact time it was present.
• Demon Eye. As a Magic action, you gain the ability to see 
through solid objects out to a range of 15 feet. This vision is 
blocked by 1 foot of stone, dirt, or wood; 1 inch of metal; or a 
thin sheet of lead.
Fish. While wearing this mask, you gain a Swim Speed equal  
to your Speed and the ability to breathe underwater. 
Additionally, you always have the Water Bullet and Whelm 
Weapon spells prepared.
Fox. While wearing this mask, you can move through an 
enemy’s space (regardless of its size), and that enemy's space 
isn't Difficult Terrain for you. Additionally, your AC increases by 1, 
and when you make a Dexterity saving throw, you can take a 
Reaction to gain Advantage on the roll.
Golem (Prerequisite: Level 5+ Bard). While wearing this mask, 
your attacks with weapons and Unarmed Strikes deal an extra 
1d8 damage on a hit, and the Heavy property doesn’t impose 
Disadvantage on your attack rolls with Heavy weapons, even if 
your Strength or Dexterity score is less than 13. In addition, your 
attacks and spells deal double damage to objects and structures.
Harpy (Prerequisite: Level 11+ Bard). While wearing this mask, 
you have a Fly Speed equal to your Speed and Resistance to 
Psychic damage.
Old Man. While wearing this mask, you always have the Detect 
Magic* and Identify* spells prepared, and you can cast them 
without expending a spell slot or Material components.
Protagonist. When you roll Initiative while wearing this mask, 
you gain Temporary Hit Points equal to half your Bard level 
(round up). Additionally, you can take a Bonus Action to mark a 
creature as your antagonist for 1 minute. For the duration, you 
have Advantage on ability checks involving your antagonist. 
When you see your antagonist make an attack roll—but before 
the GM says whether the attack hits or misses—you can take a 
Reaction to expend a use of Bardic Inspiration; roll your Bardic 
Inspiration die and subtract the number rolled from your 
antagonist’s attack roll.
Sea Urchin. While wearing this mask, you can take a Bonus 
Action and expend a use of Bardic Inspiration, rolling a Bardic 
Inspiration die. You regain a number of Hit Points equal to the 
number rolled plus half your Bard level (round up).
Additionally, you can take a Magic action to attempt to 
immobilize a creature you can see within 30 feet of you, injecting 
it with magical toxins. The target must succeed on a Constitution 
saving throw or have the Restrained condition for 1 minute. The 
target repeats the save at the end of each of its turns, ending the 
effect on itself on a success. You can use this ability a number of 
times equal to your Charisma modifier (minimum of once). You 
regain all expended uses when you finish a Long Rest.
Spirit (Prerequisite: Level 7+ Bard). While wearing this mask, 
you always have the Speak with Dead* spell prepared. 
Additionally, you can expend a use of Bardic Inspiration to 
temporarily move through the Spirit Realm. When you move in 
this way, you step through the veil into the Spirit Realm where it 
overlaps with your current plane. 
While in the Spirit Realm, you can affect and be affected only 
by creatures, objects, and effects on that plane. Creatures that 
aren't in the Spirit Realm can’t perceive or interact with you 
unless a feature gives them the ability to do so. At the end of 
your turn or when you stop moving, you return to the plane you 
left in the spot that corresponds to your space in the Spirit 
Realm. If you appear in an occupied space, you are shunted to 
the nearest unoccupied space and take 1d10 Force damage.
Stone. While wearing this mask, you gain proficiency in the 
Athletics skill, and all Bludgeoning, Piercing, and Slashing 
damage you take is reduced by 2. Additionally, you have 
Advantage on ability checks and saving throws against  
effects that would push or pull you or cause you to have  
the Prone condition.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

CIRCLE OF THE  
PETAL DRUID 
In the tranquil groves where nature's harmony sings loudest, 
there exists a circle of Druids attuned to the delicate dance of 
petals upon the breeze. These Druid guardians of the natural 
world, known as the Circle of the Petal, draw their power from 
the spirit of Obojima, the steady island breeze, and the 
ephemeral beauty and resilience of flowers. Embracing these 
subtle forces, they harness the whispers of the wind and the 
gentle caress of petals to weave their enchantments and shape 
the world around them.
Members of the Circle of the Petal are revered for their deep 
connection to the sacred dawn petal tree and their ability to 
evoke its serene splendor in both peaceful sanctuaries and dire 
situations. These Druids become conduits of life energy, 
channeling the essence of blossoms into healing balms, 
protective barriers, and devastating bursts of floral fury. Guided 
by the eternal cycle of growth, bloom, and decay, they embody 
the ever-renewing vitality of nature, ensuring that even in the 
darkest of times, hope blossoms anew like petals on the wind.
Level 3: Petal Dance
You become permeated with the spirit of Obojima and gain the 
ability to control a fraction of Obojima’s magic, which manifests 
as flower petals of your choosing. As a Bonus Action, you can 
expend a use of Wild Shape to call on this power, conjuring a 
resilient cloud of petals that functions as an extension of your 
own being. The cloud lasts for 1 hour. While enveloped by it, you 
have a +1 bonus to your AC, and you gain the following benefits:
As a Bonus Action, you can cause your petals to lunge toward a 
creature you can see within 30 feet of you, slashing at its body. 
Make a ranged spell attack against the target using your spell 
attack bonus. On a hit, the target takes 1d6 Slashing damage. This 
damage increases by 1d6 when you reach Druid levels 5 (2d6), 11 
(3d6), and 17 (4d6).
When you or a creature you can see within 10 feet of you takes 
damage, you can take a Reaction to reduce the damage by an 
amount equal to your Druid level plus your Wisdom modifier. 
Once used in this way, the cloud dissipates.
Level 6: Petal Beast Mimicry
You gain the ability to imbue life into your petals. As a Magic 
action, you can summon a spirit that takes the appearance of an 
animal of your choice. This spirit arrives as a great wind that 
overtakes the petals before transforming into the desired beast, 
which you control. The spirit uses the Wild Spirit stat block.
The spirit appears in an unoccupied space of your choice within 
30 feet of you and acts on your turn. It can only take the Dash and 
Attack actions. If the spirit is reduced to 0 Hit Points, it explodes 
in a stunning spectacle of cascading petals. When this happens, 
each creature within a 20-foot Emanation originating from the 
spirit is affected by the Faerie Fire* spell until the end of your 
next turn. Otherwise, the spirit disappears after 1 minute or if 
you dismiss it early (no action required).
You have two uses of this feature, and you gain an 
additional use of it when you reach Druid levels 11 
(three uses) and 16 (four uses). You regain all 
expended uses of this feature when you finish a Long 
Rest. Starting at Druid level 11, you can expend two 
uses of this feature to summon two Wild Spirits 
instead of one when you take this action.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 10: Spirit of Obojima
The spirit of Obojima comes to your aid in both subtle and grand 
ways. You have Advantage on Wisdom (Survival) checks to find a 
path or creature, as the wind carries a collection of brilliant 
white petals in the direction you seek.
Additionally, you can take a Magic action to create a wall of 
petals in a space you can see. You can make the wall up to 60 feet 
long, 15 feet high, and 1 foot thick. It appears in any orientation 
you choose, as a horizontal or vertical barrier or at an angle. It 
can be free floating or resting on a solid surface. If the wall cuts 
through a creature’s space when it appears, the creature is pushed 
to one side of the wall (you choose which side).
Nothing can physically pass through the wall except for 
creatures you designate. It has Immunity to all damage, as the 
petals instantaneously heal any hole that would be created by an 
attack or effect. This wall lasts for a number of minutes equal to 
your Druid level or until you dismiss it early (no action required).
Once you create the petal barrier, you can’t do so again until 
you finish a Long Rest.
Level 14: Winds of Revival 
The spirit of Obojima comes to your aid in times of greatest 
need. When you are reduced to 0 Hit Points, you instead regain a 
number of Hit Points equal to half your Hit Point maximum and 
are lifted to your feet amidst a turbulent tempest of petals.
You can then immediately take a Reaction to send a wave of 
concussive wind sweeping out from you. Each creature in a 
10-foot Emanation originating from you must make a Strength 
saving throw against your Druid spell save DC. On a failed save, 
a creature takes 2d8 Slashing damage and is pushed 15 feet away 
from you.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you finish 
a Long Rest.

SPIRIT-FUSED FIGHTER
Even the life of a spirit must come to an end.
Those who take on the moniker of a Spirit-Fused Fighter do 
not normally do so by choice but rather by circumstance. To 
become a Spirit-Fused Fighter, you must first become the vessel 
of a dying spirit—a process that can’t be sought after willingly, as 
no one truly understands how or why this occurs.
All that is known is that the spirit's mind and body have 
passed on, and its essence now coexists within the Fighter, 
granting them abilities beyond those of a normal spirit. Those 
who harness this power can channel its latent energy into 
objects, which produce a magical quirk or powerful attacks. 
These arcane tricks are how these unconventional warriors fight 
and are the reason they have garnered so much attention and 
interest on the island.
Level 3: Arcane Quirk
As the host of a powerful spirit, the magic within you can be 
strange and unruly. Though you’ve learned to control your 
powers, the arcane energy can still spark to life, often creating 
strange effects.
Choose one or more of the Arcane Quirks listed below:
When activating any feature from this subclass, First Age 
technology around you begins to go haywire. 
Whenever you make an attack roll with a weapon or an Unarmed 
Strike, a radio or cassette player on your person plays a snippet 
of a song.
• Whenever you take damage, you cough bubbles.
• Spirits find your odor to be incredibly off-putting.
• Spirits find your odor to be incredibly attractive.
• While you have the Unconscious condition, your body  
floats 1 foot off the ground and can be carried by the wind.
• Whenever you score a Critical Hit against a creature, your 
head randomly transforms into a strange visage (such as an 
anthropomorphic pig head, a crimson-skinned version of 
yourself with flaming locks, the face of an Urugama, or 
a CRT TV). This transformation lasts until you transform 
again or finish a Long Rest.
Level 3: Channel Essence
You gain the ability to channel spirit energy into your attacks. You 
have four Essence Dice, which are d6s. When you make an attack 
roll using a weapon or an Unarmed Strike against a creature, you 
can expend an Essence Die and roll it. Add the number rolled to 
the attack roll or damage roll (your choice). You can choose to do 
this either before or after making the attack roll.
You regain all expended Essence Dice when you finish a Short 
or Long Rest. You gain an additional Essence Die when you reach 
Fighter levels 7 (five dice total), 10 (six dice total), 15 (seven dice 
total), and 18 (eight dice total).
Level 3: Object Channeling
You gain proficiency in the Salvage skill. In addition, you gain the 
ability to channel your internal spirit energy into objects, creating 
an array of effects. You learn one Channeling Option of your 
choice from the “Channeling Options” section later in this 
subclass’s description. You also gain an object of your choice that 
you can use to channel the option through.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 7: Spirit Battery
You also gain the Spirit creature type, and you learn the Jolt 
cantrip. Constitution is your spellcasting ability for it. When you 
target a machine with the spell, the machine is powered for 1 
hour instead of 18 seconds.
Additionally, once on each of your turns when you hit a target 
with an attack roll using a weapon or an Unarmed Strike as part 
of the Attack action, you can replace the attack’s damage with 


--- PAGE BREAK ---

that of the Jolt cantrip. When you do so, you roll the Jolt cantrip’s 
damage dice (which deals Lightning damage) instead of the 
weapon’s damage dice; you don’t gain any additional benefits to 
the attack’s damage from other features or effects.
Level 7:  
Improved Object Channeling
You learn another Channeling Option of your choice. You can now 
use your Object Channeling feature a number of times equal to 1 
plus your Constitution modifier (minimum of twice). You regain 
all expended uses when you finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 10: Improvised Armor
You learn to channel your energy into objects you are wearing, 
causing them to become harder than steel for a brief moment. 
When you are hit by an attack roll, you can take a Reaction to 
expend one Essence Die and add the number rolled to your AC 
against that attack, potentially causing it to miss you.
Level 15: Backup Battery
You learn to draw on the spirit energy within you to gain a quick 
rush of energy. You gain an additional use of your Second Wind 
(5 uses total). In addition, when your Hit Points drop below a 
number equal to your Fighter level, you can use your Second 
Wind immediately (no action required).
Level 18: Junk Master
You learn another Channeling Option of your choice. In addition, 
when you roll Initiative, you regain expended uses of your Object 
Channeling feature until you have two if you have fewer than that.
CHANNELING OPTIONS
The channeling options are presented in alphabetical order.
Ballooning Bag. As a Bonus Action, you cause a bag you are 
wearing or carrying (such as a backpack, canvas sack, fanny pack, 
or satchel) to rapidly inflate with air. The bag then floats upward, 
lifting you off the ground and carrying you up to 30 feet straight 
into the air. You hover in place there until you let go of the bag 
(no action required) or until the start of your next turn, at which 
point the bag gently floats back to the ground.
Alternatively, while you’re falling, you can take a Reaction to 
cause the bag to inflate, granting you the benefits of the Feather 
Fall* spell.
Entangling Cord. When you take the Attack action, you can 
choose to replace one of your attacks with an entangling strike. 
Choose an object that features tendril-like properties (such as a 
chain, extension cord, game controller, rope, or tape measure). 
The object must be on your person or within 30 feet of you, and 
you must be able to see it.
When you do so, the object springs to life, stretching out toward 
a creature you can see within 15 feet of it. Make a ranged attack 
using your Constitution modifier plus your Proficiency Bonus. On  
a hit, the target is pulled up to 15 feet toward the object.
Find the Thing. As a Magic action, you focus your energy 
through a navigational object you’re touching (such as a 
compass, GPS device, or map). When you do so, you cast the 
Locate Object* spell with the following changes:
• It doesn’t require Concentration.
• It has a duration of 1 hour.
• It can detect an object within 1 mile of you, instead  
of 1,000 feet.
First Age Steed. You enact a ritual that creates a bond with a 
special vehicle of your choice that can’t fly (such as a bicycle, 
moped, or similar object you can sit on). This vehicle can only 
carry one creature and has a Speed of 60 feet. As a Magic action, 
you can summon that vehicle to your side. While summoned, the 
vehicle has Immunity to all damage. It disappears in a puff of 
smoke after 1 hour.
Goggled Vision. While wearing an ocular covering (such as ski 
goggles, spectacles, sunglasses, or a welding mask), you can take 
a Magic action to gain Darkvision with a range of 60 feet. 
Additionally, you have Advantage on Intelligence (Investigation) 
checks to determine whether something is an illusion. These 
effects on your covering last for 1 hour.
Leaping Sneakers. While wearing a pair of footwear (such as 
boots or shoes), you can take a Bonus Action to add a spring to 
your step. For 1 hour, you gain the benefits of the Jump* spell.
Pocket Voice. You can 
spend 1 minute enacting a 
ritual that binds your voice 
to an object you can see 
that looks as if it would 
produce a sound (such as  
a boombox, jewelry box, 
pair of headphones, 
portrait of a person, radio, 
or statue with a mouth). 
Your voice remains bound 
to the object for 1 hour or 
until you dismiss the effect 
as a Bonus Action. While 
bound, everything you say 
can also be heard through 
the object, provided you’re  
on the same plane of 
existence as it.
Water Jettison. As a Bonus Action, you spray a misty stream of 
water from a container on your person (such as a soda can, spray 
bottle, squirt water bottle, or waterskin). When you do so, you 
gain the benefits of the Disengage action and are pushed 10 feet 
in a direction of your choice.

SHEEP DRAGON 
SHEPHERD
The sheep dragon is often regarded as the epitome of goodness 
and authenticity on the island. These creatures are dedicated to 
freedom and unwavering kinship. Those shepherds who live and 
train among the wandering sheep dragons learn to care deeply 
for those around them and understand how a flock works 
together to overcome obstacles. They must be ready to flee to 
safety yet know when to defend their herd. The role of a Sheep 
Dragon Shepherd requires resilience, compassion, and a kind 
heart. Because of this, these Monks are regarded by the people  
of Obojima as heroic—sometimes even mythic—figures.
Historic Past
As the tale goes, the first Sheep Dragon Shepherd was a wind 
spirit who went by the name Ventu. The spirit lived among the 
grass and called all that grazed the central fields of Obojima their 
friend. Of those creatures, none pleased Ventu more than the 
playful sheep dragon. In time, Ventu and the sheep dragon 
became inseparable. The seasons would speed away, and still the 
pair would frolic and parade the Gale Fields with careless glee. It 
was during this time that people say Ventu gifted the sheep 
dragon the ability to fly and control the winds.
One day, as Ventu explored the fields, they noticed something 
unsettling in the distance: a great pillar of black smoke split the 
horizon in two. Ventu rushed across the rolling hills, only to be 
met by terrible disaster. A raging fire had scorched the southern 
fields and was slowly crawling northward. Ventu, heartbroken at 
the thought of what might become of the sheep dragon just 
beyond the hillside, made the heroic choice to stand against the 
inferno on their own.
To this day, it's unknown what became of Ventu, but 
the majestic sheep dragon stands as a testament to their 
kindness and bravery. 


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 3: Herding Sheep
You gain proficiency with Shepherd Crooks if you don’t already 
have it, and they are considered to have the Light property for 
you. You also gain the ability to herd your allies, calling them 
closer or moving them out of danger. As a Bonus Action, you can 
spend 1 or more Focus Points to cause a willing creature you can 
see within 60 feet of you to move toward you or in any other 
direction. This movement doesn’t provoke Opportunity Attacks.  
If the creature moves toward you, it can move up to 15 feet per 
Focus Point spent; if it moves in any other direction, it can move 
up to 10 feet per Focus Point spent. A creature can’t move in this 
way more than a number of feet equal to its Speed.
The number of creatures you can target with this ability 
increases when you reach Monk levels 6 (2 creatures),  
11 (3 creatures), and 17 (4 creatures).
Level 6: Wind Shot
You gain the ability to mimic the sheep dragon's Wind Pistol, 
blasting enemies with powerful gale forces at a distance. 
Whenever you would make an Unarmed Strike, you can instead 
choose to make a special ranged attack, firing a compressed 
blast of air from your mouth. This attack has a range of 60 feet 
and uses the same attack bonus and damage die as your 
Unarmed Strike.
Additionally, when you hit a target with this special attack, you 
can choose to spend 1 Focus Point to force the target to make a 
Strength saving throw. On a failed save, the target is pushed 10 
feet away from you or has the Prone condition (your choice).
Level 6: Intercepting Maneuver
Your protective nature manifests as moments of skillful deflection 
to aid a nearby ally. When an ally within 10 feet of you is hit by an 
attack roll, you can take a Reaction and spend 1 Focus Point to 
reduce the damage it takes by an amount equal to one roll of 
your Martial Arts die plus your Dexterity modifier.
Level 11: Take to the Skies
You’ve mastered a unique technique that lets you glide on the 
wind, just like a majestic sheep dragon. Whenever you use Step 
of the Wind, you also gain a Fly Speed equal to your Speed until 
the end of your turn.
Additionally, when you use Step of the Wind, you can 
simultaneously take both the Disengage and Dash actions 
without expendin a Focus Point.
Level 17: Guide to the Herd
Your vigilant watch over your companions while in the midst of 
combat allows you to give them cues on when to raise their 
defenses. Whenever you use Patient Defense to take both the 
Disengage and Dodge actions, you can spend 1 additional Focus 
Point to share that benefit with your allies. Each ally within 30 
feet of you who can see or hear you can immediately take a 
Reaction to also gain the benefits of the Disengage and Dodge 
actions until the start of your next turn.

OATH OF THE RIVER
Those who commit themselves to the Oath of the River have 
found guidance in the shifting waters and the great creatures that 
live within them. These diverse individuals model their lives and 
the tenets they follow after the tranquil waters of a blue pool 
and the rushing rapids that spill over a great waterfall—always 
striving to flow around obstacles if possible, but ready to crash 
through them when left with no other option. As the 
river flows and bends, it seeks the path of least 
resistance on its journey to the ocean. Like the 
river, Paladins who have sworn this oath remain 
adaptable but steadfast in their own course.
These Paladins share the following tenets:
• Forgiveness can be as sharp as any blade.
• Judgment is reserved for those truly deserving of it.
• If I must battle, I will fight with all my passion  
and strength.
• I will not abandon my duty, especially when others  
are counting on me.
Historic Mythos
If the stories passed down by generations of Paladins are true, 
the first of the noble warriors and sages to dedicate themselves 
to the Tenets of the River did so only after speaking with the four 
great river spirits: Din, Yon, Mu, and Go. As the story goes, the 
warrior traveled across Obojima and into the domains of the 
great rivers, where they spent many years as the river spirits’ 
yoriki. When the time came for the warrior to leave, they asked 
the four great river spirits to each bestow a piece of wisdom they 
could take back to the Physical Realm. The words spoken by the 
spirits would go on to shape the Tenets of the River.
River Shrine
River Shrines—or River Graves, as some call them—are statues 
erected in honor of a warrior, poet, or sage who followed the 
Tenets of the River. The practice is less common than it once 
was, but during the Human Age, when the first groups of 
humans began to practice them, it was customary to create 
statues for the most impactful adherents. These statues often 
depict aquatic creatures, serving as symbolic representations of 
how the deceased lived their lives. 
Bladeless 
As the Tenets of the River became more widely known, the trend 
of the bladeless warrior began to emerge. These paladins, unlike 
other swordsmen, sought to follow their beliefs without the use 
of a weapon. This way of thinking naturally lent itself to a 
slower, more contemplative lifestyle, which is why most 
attribute the founding  of the Western River Shrine and the 
northern temples to the bladeless warriors.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 3: Blessed Pool
As a Bonus Action, you can speak gentle yet courageous words 
that encourage your allies and heal them. Choose a number of 
creatures up to twice your Charisma modifier (minimum of 2) that 
you can see within 30 feet of you. Each target regains 2d6 Hit 
Points. Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 3:  
Oath of the River Spells
The magic of your oath ensures you always have certain spells 
ready; when you reach a Paladin level specified in the Oath of 
the River Spells table, you thereafter always have the listed  
spells prepared.
Level 3: Rushing Rapids
As a Magic action, you can expend one use of your Channel 
Divinity to cause a forceful wave of water to erupt outward in a 
20-foot Emanation originating from you. Each Large or smaller 
creature of your choice in the area must succeed on a Strength 
saving throw or be pushed to an unoccupied space that is 5 feet 
outside the area.
Level 7: Aura of the River
You emanate an aura that causes the area around you to feel as if 
wading through a body of water, slowing down your enemies as 
they approach. The area within your Aura of Protection is 
Difficult Terrain for other creatures. You can designate any 
number of creatures you can see to be unaffected by it  
(no action required).
In addition, the first time you hit a Large or smaller creature on 
your turn with a melee attack roll, you can use your aura to  
move the target up to 10 feet to a space you choose, provided  
it's unoccupied.
Level 15: Shielding Spirit
Whenever you make a Dexterity saving throw, you can take a 
Reaction to halve any damage you would take from the effect. 
When you do so, you can also expend a spell slot to extend this 
benefit to nearby allies. Choose a number of creatures within 10 
feet of you equal to the level of the spell slot expended; the 
damage is also halved for each of those creatures.
Level 20: Form of the River
You can manifest the powerful visage of the river spirit around 
your body. As a Bonus Action, you gain the following benefits  
for 1 minute:
• Your Speed increases by 15 feet, and you gain a Swim  
Speed of 60 feet.
• You have Advantage on all saving throws.
• Whenever you successfully move a creature with your aura,  
you can choose to deal 2d8 Bludgeoning damage to it.
Once you use this Bonus Action, you can’t use it again until you 
finish a Long Rest. You can also restore your use of it by 
expending a level 5 spell slot (no action required).

SIDE-EFFECTS  
CAUSED BY THE CORRUPTION
• Bursts of Anger  
You have sudden and passionate bursts of 
anger caused by moments of adrenaline.
• Below the Depths  
A thick steam begins to ripple off of your  
body when you've been gravely injured. The 
effects leave your clothing drenched and 
smelling of seawater.
• Withered Lungs  
You can't help but cough blood  
throughout your day.
• Flavorless  
You've lost the ability to taste.
• Sleepless Nights  
More often than not, you spend your nights 
awake, plagued by your illness.
• Vertigo  
The strong and sudden sensation of the world 
spinning around you comes on at a moment's 
notice. You're unsure as to what causes it, but 
it can be debilitating.
CORRUPTED RANGER
You have become afflicted by the mysterious illness that haunts the island, known as the Corruption. This same foul magic, which has 
stained the coastlines black, now resides within your body. It curses your skin and seeps from your pores, and in time, it will even 
become difficult to distinguish you from it.
How this has happened is your story to tell. You may have been one of the first responders to the Corruption when it came to the 
shores of Obojima, leaving you to possibly be the only survivor of that brave band of Rangers. Or perhaps you were an explorer who 
stumbled upon a pocket of Corruption and became infected or maybe you were afflicted by the Corruption due to an evil Witch’s curse.
However this fate has befallen you, you are now both cursed and empowered by the Corruption’s rotting, withering magic that is 
slowly taking over you bit by bit, replacing your own flesh with its unearthly power.
As a corrupted being, you must choose your future wisely. It's hard to say what this illness will manifest in you.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 3: First Manifestation
Whenever you take damage, you also receive a curse marker;  
if the damage was from a Critical Hit, you receive two curse 
markers instead. These markers remain active until the end of 
your next turn. The maximum number of curse markers you can 
have at a time is 2. When you hit a creature with an attack roll 
using a weapon or an Unarmed Strike, all curse markers you 
have are consumed, dealing an extra 1d4 Necrotic damage to the 
target for each curse marker consumed.
Alternatively, you can take a Bonus Action to call upon your 
corruption, immediately gaining curse markers until you have 
your maximum.
Your maximum number of curse markers increases when you 
reach Ranger levels 5 (3 markers total), 11 (4 markers total), and 
17 (5 markers total).
Level 3: Second Manifestation
When you make a Strength or Dexterity check, you can choose to 
replace the result with a number equal to 10 plus your Ranger 
level. You can wait until after you roll the d20 before deciding to 
use this feature, but you must decide before the GM says whether 
the roll succeeds or fails. You can use this feature twice, and you 
regain all expended uses when you finish a Long Rest.
Level 7: Third Manifestation
When you make an attack roll using a weapon or an Unarmed 
Strike against a creature, you can expend one curse marker to roll 
a d4 and add it to the roll. You can choose to use a curse marker 
in this way before or after making the attack roll. You can expend 
a curse marker in this way only once per turn.
Additionally, whenever you take damage, you can take a 
Reaction to reduce the damage taken by an amount equal to 
your Ranger level. Once you reduce damage in this way, you 
can’t do so again until you finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 11: Fourth Manifestation
Your ailment is beginning to have side effects on your body. 
You gain one ailment of your choice, as described below.
FAILING LUNGS
Your lungs have begun to ache, and at times you feel yourself 
gasping for air. As a Magic action, you pull your next breath from 
a creature you can see. The target can’t take Reactions until the 
start of your next turn, and if it is Large or smaller, it has the 
Prone condition. Additionally, all of your curse markers are 
consumed, dealing 1d4 Necrotic damage to the target per  
curse marker.
Alternatively, you can give your breath to another creature. 
Whenever a creature you can see makes a Dexterity saving 
throw, you can take a Reaction to give it Advantage on the save 
and increase its Speed by 15 feet until the start of your next turn.
GRAYING VISION
The world around you begins to lose some of its colorful luster. 
You gain Blindsight *with a range of 15 feet. In addition, you 
automatically detect visual illusions you can see if the DC for the 
Intelligence (Investigation) check to discern them is less than or 
equal to your Ranger spell save DC.
LOSING FEELING
Your hands and arms burn with a cold, ethereal flame that only 
you can see. As a Bonus Action, you can target a creature you can 
see within 60 feet of you, enveloping it with the same cursed 
flames. When you deal damage with your curse markers to a 
creature enveloped by these flames, each curse marker deals 1d6 
Necrotic damage instead of 1d4.
Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you 
finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 15: Fifth Manifestation 
As a Bonus Action, you can gain the following benefits until the 
start of your next turn:
• Your Speed is doubled.
• You gain a +2 bonus to AC.
• You can make two additional attacks if you take the Attack 
action.
• All of your attacks are treated as if you have your maximum 
number of curse markers.
If you use this feature a second time before finishing a Long Rest, 
in addition to the effects wearing off at the start of your next turn, 
you also gain 1 Exhaustion level and immediately drop to 1 Hit 
Point if you have more than that at the start of your turn.
Once you use this feature a second time, you can’t use it again 
until you finish a Long Rest.

WAXWORK ROGUE
Waxwork Rogues have a long history on Obojima of dealing with 
the dangerous and the arcane. They’re known for having an 
array of tools and tricks to delve into the most perilous places—
and almost always return with treasures and tales. To a 
Waxwork Rogue, any challenge can be solved with a bit of  
wax, a pinch of smarts, and a whole lot of magic.
The Waxwork Rogue offers a blend of arcane manipulation 
and roguish cunning, making them far more than just 
skilled thieves. Their abilities stem from an arcane 
heritage deeply tied to witchcraft. Waxwork Rogues 
learn unique enchantments that allow them to craft 
magical candles with diverse effects—from healing 
allies and detecting spirits to conjuring flammable wax 
barriers or wielding a whip of pure flame. This versatility 
allows them to serve as infiltrators, investigators, and even 
battlefield controllers, always adapting to challenges with their 
peculiar brand of wax-and-fire magic.
In the Beginning
The Courier Brigade was created to carry packages between 
villages and guard merchant wagons through treacherous areas. 
But there are some areas on Obojima that are rife with the 
arcane, spirit dangers, and uncanny occurrences.
Legend says that it was Lydia Starwright, Courier Brigade First 
Class, who—against all advice—sought out the aid of a powerful 
witch who was rumored to live within a hut of melted wax deep 
within the Land of Hot Water. It was there, in that melted hut, 
that the witch taught Lydia the arcane practices known only to 
certain spirits of the island, the ability to enchant wax and fire in 
wondrous ways. This knowledge transformed Lydia into the first 
Waxwork Rogue. 
Lydia brought back this knowledge to the Courier Brigade and 
formed the Waxworks Division, a dedicated group of arcane 
Rogues who volunteered for the most perilous assignments and 
deliveries of the Courier Brigade.
In the present day, Waxwork Rogues have transcended the 
ranks of the Courier Brigade, and their skills are practiced across 
the island.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 3: Conjure Flame
You know the Dancing Lights* cantrip (the lights appear as 
floating candles) and the Produce Flame* cantrip. Your 
spellcasting ability for these spells is Intelligence or Charisma 
(choose when you gain this feature).
Level 3: Wax Enchantments
You have the ability to pull and manipulate magic from the Spirit 
Realm. You learn wax enchantments that are fueled by a special 
resource called Wick Points.
Enchantments. You learn four enchantments of your choice from 
the “Enchantment Options” section below. You learn two 
additional enchantments of your choice when you reach Rogue 
levels 9, 13, and 17. Each time you learn new enchantments, you 
can also replace one enchantment you know with a different one.
Wick Points. You have 3 Wick Points. Your maximum number of 
Wick Points increases by 1 whenever you gain a Rogue level. 
When you expend a Wick Point, it is unavailable until you finish a 
Short or Long Rest, at the end of which you regain all your 
expended points.
Level 9: Burn Cycle
You can ignite your weapons in a flash of white-hot flames when 
you successfully catch an enemy off guard. When you use your 
Sneak Attack on your turn, you can expend Wick Points in place of 
Sneak Attack dice whenever you use a Cunning Strike effect. You 
must expend 1 Wick Point per Sneak Attack die you would 
normally have to forgo. When you expend Wick Points in this way, 
you can also change the damage type of your Sneak Attack 
damage to Fire for that attack.
Level 13: Advanced 
Enchantments
Some of your enchantments become more potent; refer to the 
enhanced effects below. If you haven’t learned any of the 
following enchantments, you learn one of them as part of  
this feature.
Blooming Light. The effects of Blooming Light last for 8 hours, 
instead of 1 hour.
Bocha Glue Wax. The DC for the Strength (Athletics) check to 
break the bond early increases to 20.
Burning Delay. You can now delay the effects of the specified 
enchantments by 1 round, 3 rounds, 1 minute, 10 minutes,  
or 1 hour.
Candle Pop. Candle Pop affects the target and each creature 
within 5 feet of it.
Delicacy. The creature regains 1d12 Hit Points instead of 1d6, and 
you can have up to four candles with this enchantment at a time 
instead of two.
Iron Seal. The DC for the Strength (Athletics) check to break the 
seal increases to 20.
Maker’s Mark. Maker’s Mark now deals Bludgeoning damage 
equal to 1d6 plus your Dexterity modifier, plus an extra 1d10  
Fire damage.
Shielding Seal. You can have up to 3 Shielding Seals active at  
a time instead of 1.
Waxlings. As a Magic action, you can create two Waxlings 
simultaneously by spending 3 Wick Points instead of 2.
Level 17: Spirit Flame
You learn to craft a special candle made of pink wax. As a Bonus 
Action, you can ignite this candle, which burns for 1 minute. 
While the burning candle is on your person, you gain the 
following benefits:
• The Wick Point cost of your enchantments is  
reduced by 1.
• You have Immunity to Fire damage.
• Spirits have Disadvantage on attack rolls against you.
• The candle can’t be extinguished by nonmagical means.
Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you finish  
a Long Rest.

be done with it 
including the 
Spirit Flame 
special candle.

ENCHANTMENT OPTIONS
The enchantments are presented in alphabetical order.
Blooming Light. As a Magic action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to 
ignite a dark green candle, which burns in a similar hue for 1 
hour. While lit, the candle sheds Dim Light in a 10-foot radius. 
Creatures in the candle’s light are hidden from Divination magic 
and can’t be targeted by such magic or perceived through magical 
scrying sensors.
Bocha Glue Wax. Bocha glue is a delicate mixture of the finest 
waxes available and a collection of ingredients known only to the 
Waxwork Rogues. When enchanted properly, it can temporarily 
hold any two objects together. As a Magic action, you can spend 1 
Wick Point to create an adhesive bond between two objects using 
just a small amount of bocha glue. The two objects remain bound 
for 24 hours, after which the enchantment fades and they 
separate. A creature within reach of the objects can take a Utilize 
action to make a DC 15 Strength (Athletics) check, breaking the 
bond early on a success.
Burning Delay. You can spend 3 additional Wick Points to 
simultaneously activate Burning Delay when you use one of the 
following enchantments: Candle Pop, Fish Fat Candle, or 
Detonate. When you do so, you delay that enchantment’s 
activation by 1 round, 1 minute, or 10 minutes (your choice).
Candle Pop. As a Bonus Action, you can spend 2 Wick Points to 
ignite a misshapen yellow candle and hurl it at a creature you 
can see within 60 feet of you. The target must succeed on a 
Dexterity saving throw against your Cunning Strike DC or be 
partially encased in wax, causing the target to have the 
Restrained condition. At the end of each of its turns, the 
Restrained target repeats the save, ending the effect on itself  
on a success.
Consuming Flame (Prerequisite: Level 9+ Rogue). When you 
see an enemy within 60 feet of you casting a spell, you can take a 
Reaction and spend 3 Wick Points to momentarily ignite a thin 
white candle and cast Counterspell*, using your Cunning Strike 
DC. If the spell is successfully countered and was level 3 or lower, 
you can spend an additional 2 Wick Points to store the spell 
inside your candle.
While holding the candle, you can reignite it to cast the spell 
stored inside, using the spell’s normal casting time. The spell 
uses the slot level, spell save DC, spell attack modifier, and 
spellcasting ability of the original caster, but is otherwise treated 
as if you cast the spell. Once the spell is cast, the candle is 
sundered and becomes unusable. A spell can be stored inside a 
candle for up to 24 hours, after which the spell fades and can no 
longer be used.
Delicacy. As a Magic action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to imbue 
the tart flavor of a pyramid melon and the healing properties of a 
river spirit into a candle. As a Bonus Action, a creature can 
consume the candle to regain 1d6 Hit Points and receive enough 
nourishment to sustain it for one day. A candle holds this 
enchantment for 24 hours, after which its benefits end. You can 
have no more than two candles with this enchantment at a time.
Detonate (Prerequisite: Level 9+ Rogue). As a Magic action, you 
can spend 3 or more Wick Points to ignite a dark black candle and 
throw it at a point you can see within 60 feet of you. Each 
creature in a 20-foot-radius Sphere centered on that point must 
make a Dexterity saving throw against your Cunning Strike DC, as 
a brilliant eruption of flame sweeps out from it. For 3 Wick Points, 
a target takes 2d6 Fire damage and 2d8 Thunder damage on a 
failed save or half as much damage on a successful one. You can 
increase this enchantment’s Fire damage by 1d6 for each 
additional Wick Point you spend. Flammable objects in the area 
that aren't being worn or carried start burning.
Fish Fat Candle. As a Magic action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to 
ignite an oily brick of blubber-infused candle wax and throw it at 
a point you can see on the ground within 60 feet of you. One 
round after the candle lands, it emits a cloud of colorful smoke 
that creates a Heavily Obscured area in a 20-foot radius centered 
on that point. The candle continues to spew smoke for 1 minute, 
creating a visible trail in the sky that can be seen from up to 10 
miles away.
Flooding Abundance. As a Magic action, you can spend 2 Wick 
Points to ignite a tea light candle and throw it into an unoccupied 
space you can see on the ground within 60 feet of you. The 
candle melts rapidly, bubbling and boiling with an overwhelming 
amount of wax, which flows over and fills a 15-foot Square 
centered on the candle. The wax remains for 1 minute, and its 
area is Difficult Terrain. It is flammable, and a 5-foot Square of 
wax exposed to fire burns away in 3 rounds, dealing 2d6 Fire 
damage to any creature that starts its turn in the fire.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Iron Seal. As a Magic action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to melt 
and press the wax seal of iron onto a door or an object with a lid. 
Once imbued with your seal, the object becomes magically held 
shut and can’t be opened unless a creature takes a Utilize action 
to make a DC 15 Strength (Athletics) check, breaking the seal on a 
success. The Iron Seal lasts until it is broken or dispelled (as if it 
were a level 1 spell). You can take a Magic action to touch one of 
your Iron Seals and end its effects early.
Lost Wax Carving. Using a lost form of wax carving, you can 
spend 2 Wick Points to craft a detailed replica of an object over the 
course of 10 minutes, producing the effects of the Duplicate spell. 
The object you duplicate must be no larger than a 1-foot Cube.
Maker’s Mark. Once on each of your turns, when you make an 
attack roll with a one-handed weapon as part of the Attack 
action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to make an Unarmed Strike 
with your free hand as part of the same action, using one of your 
signet rings. This Unarmed Strike deals Bludgeoning damage 
equal to 1d4 plus your Dexterity modifier, plus an extra 1d6 Fire 
damage. This attack can benefit from your Sneak Attack, provided 
you haven’t already used it this turn.
Shielding Seal. As a Magic action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to 
melt and press the wax seal of shielding onto a willing creature 
or an object, protecting it from incoming damage. The target 
gains 5 Temporary Hit Points, which last for 24 hours. You can 
grant an additional 5 Temporary Hit Points for each additional 
Wick Point spent, to a maximum of 15 Temporary Hit Points. You 
can have only one Shielding Seal active at a time. Creating a 
Shielding Seal while another seal of the same type is already 
active ends the effects of the initial one early.
Spark Shower. As a Bonus Action, you can spend 1 Wick Point to 
bring your free hand to your mouth, igniting your next breath. 
Your exhale creates a dazzling shower of sparks aimed at a 
creature within 5 feet of you. You have Advantage on the next 
attack roll you make with a weapon or an Unarmed Strike against 
the target this turn, and the target can’t make Opportunity Attacks 
until the end of the turn.
Waxlings. As a Magic action, you can spend 2 Wick Points to 
temporarily pull and trap a minor spirit within a candle,  
creating a Waxling. You cast the Find Familiar* spell with the 
following changes:
• In place of a normal familiar, you imbue life into the candle, 
causing it to grow appendages and eyes.
• Your Waxling familiar uses the statistics of a Rat*.
• You can command the familiar to take a Magic action to touch 
a flammable object. The object starts burning if it isn't being 
worn or carried.
• The familiar sheds Bright Light in a 5-foot radius and Dim Light 
for an additional 10 feet.
• You can’t temporarily dismiss the familiar.
• The familiar is dismissed permanently after 1 hour or when it is 
reduced to 0 Hit Points.
• You can have more than one of these familiars at a time.
Wick Whip. As a Bonus Action, you can spend 3 Wick Points to 
ignite a 10-foot length of candlewick that has soaked in the 
stomach acid of a dragon frog. The flames burn at an intense heat 
that warps the air around them, shedding Bright Light in a 15-foot 
radius and Dim Light for an additional 15 feet. The candlewick 
burns for 1 minute, during which you can use it as a Melee 
weapon you’re proficient with. It deals 3d4 Fire damage on a hit 
(add your ability modifier to the damage roll as normal), and it 
has the Finesse, Light, and Reach properties.

ONI KIN SORCERY
In the realm of magic, there exists a lineage of Sorcerers whose 
blood bears an ancient connection to the oni. These Sorcerers, 
known as Oni Kin, harness the magic of their lineage to weave 
powerful spells. But as they delve deeper into their arcane 
abilities, they find themselves gradually transforming—both 
physically and spiritually—into embodiments of the oni’s 
fearsome might.
At the outset of their journey and as they use their powers, 
Oni Kin begin to see subtle manifestations of their lineage: 
changes in appearance and temperament. However, as they 
channel their magic with greater skill, these traits begin to 
intensify. Their skin may change, their eyes may glow with an 
eerie light, and their once-subtle features may become more 
pronounced, bearing the unmistakable visage of an oni.
As their power reaches its zenith, Oni Kin reach a pinnacle 
where they can fully embrace their heritage and assume the 
form of a true oni. In this form, they stand as towering figures  
of terror, wielding unparalleled magical might and physical 
prowess. Yet with this transformation comes a perilous 
temptation—the struggle to maintain control over the oni’s 
insatiable hunger for chaos and destruction. This struggle does 
not go unnoticed by islanders, most of whom fear or distrust  
the Oni Kin.
Level 3: Oni Spells
When you reach a Sorcerer level specified in the Oni Spells table, 
you thereafter always have the listed spells prepared.
Level 3: Arcane Prison
Trapped inside you is the essence of the first oni, passed down 
through its children and stretched across a long and treacherous 
lineage. As you grow in power, so does the spirit within you. It 
desperately wishes to bubble to the surface, and it does so when 
you’re at your weakest. You gain the traits of the oni, which 
manifest as you expend Sorcery Points. Each oni trait becomes 
available to you based on how many Sorcery Points you’re 
missing from your total, as detailed in the table below. Regaining 
Sorcery Points can cause you to lose one or more oni traits.
Each oni trait has both a physical manifestation and an arcane 
effect, which last until you finish a Long Rest or otherwise lose the trait.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

ONI TRAITS
The traits are presented in the order they manifest, from least 
Sorcery Points missing to most.
Eyes. Your eyes shimmer with an almost mesmerizing quality. As 
a Magic action, you can activate your innate ocular charm. For 1 
minute, you have Advantage on all Charisma checks directed at 
one creature of your choice that isn’t Hostile toward you, provided 
it can see your eyes. When the effect ends, the creature must 
make a Wisdom saving throw against your Sorcerer spell save DC. 
On a success, the target realizes that you used magic to influence 
its mood and becomes Hostile toward you. A creature prone to 
violence might attack you. Another creature might seek 
retribution in a different way (at the GM’s discretion), depending 
on the nature of your interaction.
Horns. Horns rapidly sprout from your head. When you cast a 
cantrip that requires you to make a melee or ranged spell attack, 
you can instead make a melee spell attack using your horns, 
channeling the spell through them. When you hit a creature  
with a cantrip cast in this way, the target takes an extra 1d6 
Piercing damage.
Additionally, when a creature provokes an Opportunity Attack 
from you by leaving your reach, you can take a Reaction to cast a 
cantrip at the creature using your horns, rather than making an 
Opportunity Attack. The spell must have a casting time of an 
action and must target only that creature.
Skin. Your skin turns a dull red, green, or blue color (your 
choice), and you adopt the regenerative powers of the oni. 
Whenever you cast a spell of level 1 or higher, you regain a 
number of Hit Points equal to the spell’s level plus your 
Constitution modifier. You don’t gain this benefit if you have the 
Tongue trait active during that casting.
Tongue. With every incantation you cast, the twisted and 
demonic voice of the first oni can be heard within your speech. 
When you cast a spell that has a Verbal component and targets a 
single creature, you can also take a Bonus Action to cause the 
target to recoil in fear. The target must make a Wisdom saving 
throw against your Sorcerer spell save DC. On a failed save, the 
target either has the Prone condition or it must immediately use 
its Reaction, if available, to move up to half its Speed away from 
you (your choice).
Hair. Your hair turns a shocking white and stretches towards the 
ground as it grows to cover your back. You gain a +2 bonus to AC.
Level 6: Ogre Manipulation
You can manifest oni traits regardless of how many Sorcery Points 
you’re missing. As a Bonus Action, you can activate one of the oni 
traits you currently have access to, drawing it out early. When 
activated in this way, the trait lasts for 1 minute, and you lose it if 
you haven’t gained the trait by normal means within that time.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Long Rest.
Level 14: Boiling Power
Your oni traits grow in power. The following changes apply to 
your traits.
Eyes. In addition to the trait’s normal benefits, you have the Zone 
of Truth* spell prepared, which you can cast without expending a 
spell slot. When cast in this way, only one creature of your choice 
within 60 feet of you that can see your eyes is affected. The target 
repeats its save against the spell at the start of each of its turns; 
the spell ends early if the target can no longer see your eyes.
Horns. The extra damage dealt by your horns increases to 1d12.
Skin. Whenever you cast a spell of level 1 or higher, you now 
regain a number of Hit Points equal to twice the spell’s level plus 
your Constitution modifier.
Tongue. When you activate the Tongue trait using a spell slot of 
level 5 or higher, instead of the trait’s normal effects, you can 
cause the target to tremble in fear, becoming hyperfixated on 
you. The target’s Passive Perception is reduced to 5 and it takes a 
−5 penalty to its AC against all attacks not made by you. This 
effect lasts until the start of your next turn.
Level 18: Transformation
You can fully embody the fabled visage of your demon ancestor 
without needing to exhaust your sorcerous power. As a Magic 
action, you can instantly manifest all of your oni traits, regardless 
of how many Sorcery Points you’re missing. While manifesting 
your oni traits in this way, you have Resistance to Bludgeoning, 
Piercing, and Slashing damage, and you have Immunity to the 
Charmed and Frightened conditions.
This effect lasts for 1 minute, after which you lose any trait you 
haven’t gained by normal means in that time. Once you use this 
feature, you can’t do so again until you finish a Long Rest, unless 
you spend 5 Sorcery Points (no action required) to restore your 
use of it.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

LANTERN PATRON
Warlocks who make a pact with a powerful spirit are able to tap 
into the magic that flows through the Spirit Realm. These 
Warlocks are known by the special lanterns they carry—lanterns 
that burn with the essence of their patron. The illumination of this 
vessel carries the attributes of the spirit, granting the Warlock an 
array of abilities. 
When spirits enter pacts with people, there is often more to it 
than generosity. Spirits powerful enough to lend out bits of their 
magic do so for a variety of reasons. Perhaps the spirit is bound 
by a bargain or curse. It could be that the spirit needs allies 
(though they might not readily admit it). Or maybe they simply 
see something in you that amuses them. The things that 
motivate spirits are as varied as the spirits themselves—and truly 
powerful spirits can be inscrutable.
Level 3: Lantern Spells
The magic of your patron ensures you always have certain spells 
ready; when you reach a Warlock level specified in the Lantern 
Spells table, you thereafter always have the listed spells prepared
Level 3: Illuminating Aura
The essence of your spirit patron is channeled into a lantern, 
where it appears as a minor form of itself. You can use your 
lantern as a Spellcasting Focus for your Warlock spells. 
As a Bonus Action, you can activate your lantern, causing it to 
shed Bright Light in a 20-foot radius and Dim Light for an 
additional 20 feet. This light lasts for 1 minute, until you let go of 
the lantern, or until you choose to end the effect early (no action 
required). For the duration, you gain the following benefits:
• Whenever you see a creature in your lantern’s Bright Light 
make a saving throw, you can take a Reaction to grant that 
creature a bonus to the roll equal to your Charisma modifier 
(minimum of +1).
• Whenever an enemy within your lantern’s Dim Light fails 
a saving throw, it takes Radiant damage equal to half your 
Warlock level (round up).
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 3: Revealing Light
You can take a Magic action to cause your lantern to illuminate 
with a vibrant maroon light, which sheds Bright Light in a 10-foot 
radius and Dim Light for an additional 10 feet. Invisible creatures 
and objects are visible while they are in the lantern's Bright Light. 
The lantern sheds light in this way for 1 hour or until you end the 
effect early as a Bonus Action.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Short or Long Rest.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 6: Dangerous Tool
Your Illuminating Aura no longer ends if you let go of your 
lantern. While you aren’t holding your lantern, you can magically 
take control of it for 1 minute (no action required), using it as if it 
were a Spiritual Weapon* (cast as a level 2 spell), without 
requiring your Concentration. Your lantern continues to act as 
your Spellcasting Focus while using this feature, even though you 
are no longer holding it.
The level at which Spiritual Weapon is considered to be cast 
increases when you reach Warlock levels 10 (level 3 spell)  
and 14 (level 4 spell).
Once you take control of your lantern in this way, you  
can’t do so again until you finish a Long Rest, unless 
 you expend a Pact Magic spell slot to take control 
 of it again.
Level 6: Oracle Illumination
You can take a Magic action to connect your mind to a  
light source (such as a candle or torch) that you can see  
or are familiar with. The light source functions like the  
sensor created by the Clairvoyanc* spell, granting you the  
same benefits. You can use the light source in this way for 10  
minutes or until you use this feature again. 
Once you use this feature on a light source, you can’t use it  
on the same light source again until you finish a Long Rest.
Level 10: Brilliant Illumination
While your lantern’s Illuminating Aura is active, you can take a 
Magic action to cause the light to flare with an overwhelmingly 
brilliant flash. Each creature other than you illuminated by either 
your lantern’s Bright Light or Dim Light (your choice) must make a 
Constitution saving throw against your Warlock spell save DC. On 
a failed save, a creature takes Radiant damage equal to 2d8 plus 
your Warlock level and has the Blinded condition until the end of 
your next turn. On a successful save, the creature takes half as 
much damage only.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Short or Long Rest.
Level 14: Brighter Still
You gain the ability to activate your lantern’s Illuminating Aura at 
will. Features such as Dangerous Tool and Brilliant Illumination 
that work in conjunction with Illuminating Aura are still limited to 
the number of uses described in their respective features.
Additionally, while holding your lantern, you can take a Magic 
action to cause it to illuminate with a pale blue light. Doing so 
reveals a glowing arcane path to a location you're familiar with, 
as if you cast the Find the Path* spell.
Once you use your lantern in this way, you can’t do so again 
until you finish a Long Rest.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

ORIGAMI MAGE
Origami Mages are wielders of a unique form of magic that 
combines precision, creativity, and imagination. With a flick of the 
wrist and a whisper of arcane words, they transform simple 
sheets of paper into awe-inspiring manifestations of elemental 
forces, mystical beings, and fantastical creatures.
Drawing inspiration from the mysterious elegance of origami, 
these mages are not bound by traditional spell components but 
instead rely on the meticulous manipulation of paper to channel 
their magical energies. Origami magic is not without its 
challenges. Mastery of this arcane discipline demands patience, 
dexterity, and a keen eye for detail. Each fold must be precise, 
each crease exact—for even the smallest imperfection can disrupt 
the flow of magic and render a spell ineffective. Yet for those 
who persevere, the rewards are boundless.
Level 3: An Arcane Art
You learn to weave magic into origami, allowing you to create 
magnificent moving art pieces that act on your behalf. As a Bonus 
Action, you can fold and imbue life into a piece of paper that 
takes a form you choose from the “Origami Constructs” section 
below. When crafted, an Origami Construct becomes bound to 
you or to another creature of your choice that you can see within 
60 feet of you (your choice).
A creature with a bound Origami Construct gains the unique 
effects and benefits listed for that Construct. A creature can’t 
have more than one of the same Origami Construct bound to it at 
a time, unless stated otherwise. A bound Origami Construct 
occupies the same space as the creature it’s bound to.
These Constructs remain imbued with life for a number of 
hours equal to half your Wizard level (round up). Origami 
Constructs are objects with an AC equal to your Wizard spell 
save DC. They have Immunity to Poison and Psychic damage, and 
they are destroyed when they take any damage. You can use this 
feature to create an Origami Construct a number of times equal 
to your Intelligence modifier (minimum of once). You regain all 
expended uses when you finish a Long Rest.
ORIGAMI CONSTRUCTS
The Origami Constructs are presented in alphabetical order.
Bird. While the origami bird is bound to a creature, that creature 
gains proficiency in the Perception skill. Additionally, the creature 
deals an extra 2 Slashing damage whenever it hits a target with a 
ranged attack.
Cat. While the origami cat is bound to a creature, that creature 
gains proficiency in the Stealth skill. Additionally, once on each of 
the creature’s turns when it hits a target with a melee attack roll 
using a weapon or an Unarmed Strike, the origami cat can make 
a melee spell attack against the same target. The origami cat’s 
attack modifier is equal to the bound creature’s weapon attack 
modifier, and on a hit, the target takes 1d6 Slashing damage.
The origami cat’s damage increases when the Wizard that 
crafted it reaches levels 5 (1d8), 11 (1d10), and 17 (1d12).
Crab. While the origami crab is bound to a creature, that creature 
gains a +1 bonus to AC and proficiency in the Athletics skill. If the 
Wizard who crafted this origami crab creates another, this origami 
crab is destroyed.
Dragon. While the origami dragon is bound to a creature, that 
creature has Disadvantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks and can’t 
benefit from the Invisible condition. Additionally, the creature 
takes 1d4 Fire damage at the start of each of its turns. A creature 
can have multiple origami dragons bound to it at the same time.
When the origami dragon is destroyed, it quickly pops in an 
audible explosion, dealing 2d6 Fire damage to each creature 
within 5 feet of it.
Frog. While the origami frog is bound to a creature, that creature 
gains proficiency in the Acrobatics skill. Additionally, when the 
creature would fail a Dexterity saving throw, it can take a 
Reaction to add a bonus to the roll equal to the Intelligence 
modifier of the Wizard that crafted the origami frog (minimum of 
+1); using this effect destroys the origami frog.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

Level 3: Origami Familiar
You always have the Find Familiar* spell prepared. Your familiar 
appears as an origami version of itself. It has Immunity to Poison 
and Psychic damage as well as the Poisoned condition, and it  
is a Construct instead of a Celestial, Fey, or Fiend. In addition to 
the familiar’s normal statistics, it also gains access to the 
following abilities:
Camouflage. You can command your origami familiar to shift 
into a flattened paper form. In this form, the familiar looks nearly 
indistinguishable from a normal piece of paper. A creature that 
takes a Study action to examine the familiar can discern that it is 
a creature with a successful Intelligence (Investigation) check 
against your Wizard spell save DC. The familiar can take a Magic 
action to shift back into its origami form.
Last Resort. As a Magic action, your origami familiar can dive 
toward a creature, unfurling itself and wrapping around the 
target’s face like a sheet of paper blown by the wind. The target 
must make a Dexterity saving throw against your Wizard spell 
save DC or have the Blinded condition for 1 minute. The target or 
another creature within 5 feet of it can take an action to make a 
Strength (Athletics) check against your Wizard spell save DC.  
On a success, the familiar is removed, and the target no longer 
has the Blinded condition. When this effect ends, the familiar  
is destroyed.
Reconnaissance. As a Magic action, you can command your 
origami familiar to spy. The familiar then spends 1 minute 
listening to any and all sounds within 15 feet of itself, recording 
what it overhears on its paper body. It then returns to you and 
becomes an inert piece of paper, leaving behind a transcript of its 
findings written in a language of your choice that you know.
Level 6: Binding Release 
You can take a Bonus Action to move one of your Origami 
Constructs to a creature that you can see within 30 feet of it.
Level 6: Paper Path
When you cast a spell with a range of Touch and your  
Origami Familiar delivers the touch, it no longer requires the 
familiar’s Reaction.
Level 10: Origami Servant
You always have the Unseen Servant* spell prepared. In addition, 
you can cast it without expending a spell slot, but the maximum 
number of servants you can have at a time is equal to half  
your Wizard level (round up). When you cast it, it has the 
following changes:
• The spell lasts for a number of hours equal to 1 plus your 
Intelligence modifier (minimum of 2 hours), instead of 1 hour.
• Your servant appears as a visible origami version of itself.
• Your servant has Immunity to Poison and Psychic damage as 
well as the Poisoned condition.
• Your servant can move through a space as narrow as 1 inch 
without expending extra movement to do so.
• When you take a Bonus Action to command a servant, you can 
issue a unique command to each servant you have created as 
part of the same Bonus Action.
• Your servant falls at a rate of 60 feet per round and takes no 
damage from falling.
• Your servant can see Invisible creatures and objects as if they 
were visible.
• As a Magic action while your servant is within 200 feet of 
you, you can see through its eyes and hear what it hears until 
the start of your next turn, gaining the benefits of any special 
senses it has.
• You can command your servant to perform a task that would 
move it up to 200 feet away from you, instead of 60 feet.
Level 14: Arcane Refresh
Whenever one of your Origami Constructs is destroyed, the magic 
you lent it returns to you. You either regain 10 Hit Points or one 
expended spell slot of level 2 or lower (your choice).
Additionally, when one of your Origami Constructs you can see 
would take damage, you can take a Reaction to negate that 
damage. Once you use this ability, you can’t do so again until you 
finish a Long Rest.

the nature of Obojima and its past. With your

traveled to one or more of AHA’s excavation sites 
and worked alongside the organization, but never 
became an official member. Even now, unanswered 
questions from your time with the group continue  
to rattle around in your mind. For more on AHA,

You are, or once were, a member of the Mariners’ Guild, an 
intrepid group of aquatic explorers and mariners. Working 
as an apprentice diver in the lodge, you have learned much 
about the Shallows—you know what is dangerous and 
what is delicious. You have climbed the cliffs around the 
island, explored many beaches, swam in the waters, and 
learned how to use the gear needed to survive under the 
waves. For more on the Mariners’ Guild, see page 21.

You’ve spent most of your life working on 
mechanisms and machines. For you, understanding 
both new and old technology requires a hands-on 
approach. Through trial and error, you have learned 
to create, repair, and modify all things mechanical 
and electronic, and you have honed your eye to 
recognize useful parts among the scattered bits of 
technology that are found throughout the island.
Though everyone living on Obojima comes into contact 
with spirits to some degree, your interactions with the 
Spirit Realm have always occurred with peculiar regularity. 
All your life, you’ve had a special kinship with spirits that 
few share in. You’ve come to love their food, their culture, 
and their people more than the average material being. 
These habits have drawn fascination, suspicion, and 
confusion from locals, but that doesn’t stop them from 
enlisting your talents when spirit stuff gets weird.


--- PAGE BREAK ---

The languages spoken on Obojima all sound different because each language has its own 
mysterious origin. The croaking language of the nakudama is very different from the whispered 
language of the spirits. There are various dialects that have developed among the human villages 
around the island that sound similar having had a common ancestry, but the language of humans 
and elves compared to that of the dara or the nakudama are as different as night and day. 
Over time, Obojimans have developed their own common tongue which allows everyone  
to converse, trade, tell tales, and poke fun at one another.

gain Advantage on Stealth checks made in 
wooded areas.
